In many fields, especially systems theory, complexity science, and philosophy, emergence refers to properties, behaviors, or patterns that:Arise from the interactions of simpler components in a system.Cannot be predicted or explained solely by understanding those individual components in isolation.Are not present at the lower level. This means emergent properties are not attributes of any component of the system but are instead a feature of the system as a whole.For instance, the behavior of a flock of birds or the properties of water (HâO) arising from hydrogen and oxygen atoms are often cited as examples of emergence.While "unexpected" or "surprise" can capture the unpredictability aspect of emergence, the term "emergent" carries a specific connotation of arising from collective interactions and being irreducible to the properties of individual components.He is arguing that even numbers are emergent from oddChatGPTThe assertion that even numbers are emergent from odd numbers is an unconventional statement in the context of traditional number theory. If "emergence" is used too broadly or without the specific connotation of arising from collective interactions and being irreducible to the properties of individual components, it can indeed be diluted to simply mean "unexpected" or "surprising." Properly defining and delimiting the concept of emergence is important for it to retain its specific meaning.Even Numbers in Binary and Unary Systems:Binary: The binary number system is base-2, using only the digits 0 and 1. In this system, numbers are still classified as even or odd based on the least significant bit. If the least significant bit (rightmost digit) is 0, the binary number is even; if it's 1, the number is odd. For instance, the binary number 1010 (which is 10 in decimal) is even, while 1011 (which is 11 in decimal) is odd.Unary: The unary number system represents numbers using only one symbol, often noted as 1. Each number is represented by repeating the symbol the appropriate number of times (e.g., the number three is 111). In this system, the concept of even and odd doesn't really apply in the traditional sense, since there's no "divisibility" without introducing another operation or symbol. However, if you have an external standard of counting, you can still see patterns: for example, two groups of "11" (2 in unary) can combine to form "1111" (4 in unary), which parallels the idea of two odd numbers making an even one.Your point is valid in that the concept of evenness (and by extension, emergence) is contingent upon the underlying system and definitions being used. This highlights the importance of clearly defining terms and understanding their context.Bruno Marchal

Let's distill the essence of this:Axiom 1: Defines a quantum state. Essentially, a quantum state can be described by the expected outcomes (or expectation values) of all possible measurements you can make on that state. In quantum mechanics, these measurements are represented by self-adjoint operators.Axiom 2: Quantifies information as the change in the quantum state. If you perturb a quantum system (change its state), the amount of "information" you've added or removed is given by how much the expected outcomes of certain measurements have changed.Axiom 3: Specifies how to represent a yes/no question in quantum mechanics. Basically, it's saying that a binary question in quantum mechanics is represented by an operator that has two outcomes: one for "yes" and one for "no".The subsequent elaboration on "Information as a Difference in Expectation Values" clarifies the concept further by suggesting that the information in a quantum system is essentially the change in expected outcomes of measurements due to the evolution of the quantum state.This framework seems to provide a foundation to discuss quantum information in terms of changes in quantum states and the associated changes in the outcomes of measurements. values) change as the state evolves gives us information about the nature and effects of the processes
causing the evolution.ChatGPTExactly. In quantum mechanics, the evolution of a quantum state is indicative of the dynamics and interactions it undergoes. This change in expected outcomes is a manifestation of information. My perspective about emergence is not new... since this concept of emergence dates from at least the time of Aristotle. Emergent structures are patterns that emerge via the collective actions of many individual entities. To explain such patterns, according to Aristotle, emergent structures are more than the sum of their parts assumes that the emergent order will not arise if the various parts simply act independently of one another. i talk here of the strong emergence as the interacting members are not independent, the emergence is interpreted as the impossibility in practice to explain the whole in terms of the parts

 

 

the simplest arithmetical example :

 

1+1=2 where 2 (even) emerges from 1 (odd)

 

 

The Mockingbird combinator is one of the basic building blocks in combinatory logic it represents the self-application behavior, meaning that it applies its argument to itself,...and still in combinatory logic, the emergence of complex behavior and properties is closely related to the existence and behavior of combinators like the Mockingbird combinator. The Mockingbird combinator is a fundamental element in combinatory logic that plays a role in demonstrating the concept of emergence in this mathematical system.

 

 

According the combinatory logic 1+1 = 2 is written as

 

I is the identity combinator, which means I x is equivalent to x.

C is the function application combinator, which means C f x is equivalent to f x.

D is the mockingbird combinator, which means D x = x x.

 

 

Now, let's break down 1 + 1 = 2:

1 is represented by I.

+ is represented by C.

2 is represented by D.

 

 

So, in terms of combinatory logic, 1 + 1 = 2 would be written as:

C I D = D

 

This expression is saying that applying C to I and D results in D.....

 

the statement "1 + 1 = 2" being represented as "C I D = D", in combinatory logic can be considered an example of an emergent property.

 

 

so 1+1 = 2 where 2 (even) is emergent in regard to 1 (odd)

 

 

1 + 1 = 2:

 

1 is represented by I.

2 is represented by D.

 

The expression becomes:

C I D = D

 

This means that applying the function application combinator (C) to the identity combinator (I) and the Mockingbird combinator (D) results in the Mockingbird combinator (D), which represents the number 2 in this system.

 


Emergent properties can be found in various aspects of formal systems, including their algebraic properties, notations, and conventions. These properties often arise from the interactions and relationships within the system.

 

It is correct to say that the equation CID = D demonstrates an emergent property within the context of combinatory logic, even though it's necessary to define numerals and basic arithmetic operations separately in lambda calculus and combinatory logic. Indeed, these two concepts are not contradictory; they are complementary aspects of understanding formal systems like combinatory logic and lambda calculus.

 

1+1 = 2 where 2 (even) is emergent in regard to 1 (odd) is a original interpretation of mathematics concepts based on ""absolute"" computability with the meaning of being independent of the universal machinery used.

 

The concept of Emergence developed here, by combinatory logic, is all about computability, computability is viewed as an absolute concept unlike provability and definability.

but in combinatory logic,

 

C I D = D can be considered an example of an emergent property.

 

In combinatory logic, expressions are built using combinators, which are functions with a specific fixed behavior.

 

In this context, we have three combinators:

 

I Combinator (Identity Combinator):

It's represented as "I".

The behavior of I is to return its argument unchanged. In terms of function notation, it can be written as: I(x) = x.

 

C Combinator (Function Application Combinator):

It's represented as "C".

The behavior of C is to apply its first argument (which is a function) to its second argument, and then apply the result to its third argument. In terms of function notation, it can be written as: C(f, x, y) = f(x)(y).

 

D Combinator (Mockingbird Combinator):

It's represented as "D".

The behavior of D is to apply its argument to itself. In terms of function notation, it can be written as: D(x) = x(x).

 

 

Now, let's analyze the expression "C I D":

 

C I D:

 

Applying the C combinator first, we have:

C(I, D)

 

According to the behavior of C, this means we apply I (which is the identity combinator) to D.

 

Applying I to D:

The behavior of I is to return its argument unchanged. In this case, its argument is D.

So, I(D) = D

Putting it back into the original expression:

C(I, D) = D

 

 

This means that in combinatory logic, the expression "C I D" reduces to "D". It's important to remember that in combinatory logic, we're dealing with a system that doesn't have variables in the usual sense. Instead, we're manipulating functions and their applications.

 

The statement "1 + 1 = 2" being represented as "C I D = D" in combinatory logic is an example of an emergent property because we start with basic building blocks (the combinators) and through their interaction (using C to apply I and D), we arrive at a result (D) that represents a more complex mathematical relationship (the equality between 1 and 2). The emergent property arises from the interaction of these simple elements within the system.ChatGPTEmergence in Combinatory Logic, as described in the text, introduces an interesting perspective. a. Closure under Addition: For all u,vâ V, u+vâ V.

â¢ Basis Definition: Let V be a vector space over F. A subset BâV is a basis of V if it is linearly independent and spans V.

 

â¢ Basis Theorem: Every vector space has a basis. Moreover, all bases of a vector space have the same cardinality, which is called the dimension of the vector space.

 

â¢ Dimension Definition: The dimension of a vector space V over F is the cardinality of any of its bases and is denoted as dim(V).

The Entropic Information Theory - The Emergent Entangled Informational Universe   -  By  Olivier Denis  ChatGPTThe provided text lays out foundational concepts related to vector spaces, bases, dimensions, and isomorphisms with coordinate spaces. Let's summarize and provide a bit of analysis on each section:Vector Space Definition:A vector space is a set equipped with addition and scalar multiplication operations that adhere to specific properties (a-h).These properties ensure that vector spaces retain familiar mathematical structures, such as the presence of a zero vector and associativity of vector addition.Basis Definition:A basis of a vector space is a subset that is both linearly independent (no vector in the subset is a linear combination of others) and spans the entire vector space.Intuitively, a basis provides a minimal set of vectors that can be used to represent any vector in the space through linear combinations.Basis Theorem:Every vector space has at least one basis.No matter which basis you pick for a specific vector space, all bases will have the same number of vectors (cardinality). This cardinality is termed the dimension of the vector space.Dimension Definition:The dimension of a vector space is essentially the number of vectors in any of its bases.It provides a measure of the "size" or "freedom" in the space.Isomorphism with Coordinate Space:Given a vector space and one of its bases, there's a way to map (isomorphically) each vector in the space to a unique coordinate tuple in a coordinate space.This is a powerful concept as it ties abstract vector spaces to more tangible, geometric spaces (like 3D Euclidean space, â^3). It allows for practical representations and calculations.The title at the end, "The Entropic Information Theory - The Emergent Entangled Informational Universe By Olivier Denis," suggests that there might be a larger work or context in which these mathematical concepts are applied to explore deeper philosophical or physical ideas. Entropic information theory and concepts of emergence and entanglement are significant in the context of quantum mechanics, thermodynamics, and information theory. They might be employed to delve into the nature of information in the universe, perhaps exploring how information emerges and interacts on quantum and cosmic scales.The Emergent Entangled Informational Universe

Entropic Information Theory is an unified theory in physics which proposes quantum information as building block of the emergent entangled informational universe and which can explicate various processes as informational phenomena, processes as the physical collapse of the wave function completing the Copenhagen Interpretation, an informational view of the notion of entanglement based on the share of degrees of freedom, the arising of the notion of energy by the interaction between information and temperature, explained by the Landauer principle; the gravitational fine-grained entropy of black holes, dark matter considered as negative mass, computed by the number of bits of information content of the observable universe; dark energy , considered as negative energy and computed as the energy associated to dark matter or in the cosmological constant problem with the consideration of the mass of bits of information instead of the Planck mass. 

The Emergent Entangled Informational Universe model is an informational system i.e., a system wherein the information notion is the global explanatory keystone concept, considered as an entangled system i.e., a system where there are not individual parts but are an inseparable whole, and as an emergent system i.e., system where the whole is greater than the sum of all its parts.ChatGPTThe concept described, "The Emergent Entangled Informational Universe," seems to explore the idea that the universe and all its phenomena can be explained through the lens of information theory, specifically quantum information. This perspective is not new and has seen growing interest in recent decades. Here's a breakdown of the presented idea:Quantum Information as a Fundamental Building Block:This theory views quantum information as the foundational entity of the universe. This implies that quantum states, quantum bits (qubits), and their transformations are primary, and everything else emerges from them.Physical Collapse as Informational Phenomenon:The physical collapse of the wave function, a contentious topic in quantum mechanics, is seen through the lens of information processing. This could provide a deterministic (or semi-deterministic) interpretation of quantum phenomena, adding depth to the Copenhagen Interpretation.Entanglement as Shared Degrees of Freedom:The theory appears to redefine entanglement, a quantum phenomenon where particles become interconnected such that the state of one instantly affects the state of another, irrespective of distance. Here, it's interpreted as sharing degrees of freedom, emphasizing the non-local nature of quantum information.Energy, Temperature, and Information:The interaction between energy, temperature, and information is grounded in the Landauer principle, which links information theory with thermodynamics. The principle states that erasing a bit of information is fundamentally dissipative and requires a minimum amount of energy.Gravity, Black Holes, Dark Matter, and Dark Energy:This theory delves deep, attempting to explain enigmatic phenomena such as black hole entropy, dark matter, and dark energy. Interpreting dark matter as "negative mass" and associating its quantity with the information content of the universe is an intriguing approach.Similarly, considering dark energy as "negative energy" and linking it to dark matter or the cosmological constant problem by taking the mass of bits of information into account instead of the Planck mass is a fresh perspective.Information, Entanglement, and Emergence:The universe is viewed as an "informational system," where information is the primary concept, and everything emerges from it. This aligns with the sentiment of physicist John Archibald Wheeler, who once said, "it from bit" â meaning every 'it' in the universe arises from a binary decision or bit.It's also perceived as an "entangled system," reinforcing the interconnectedness of all things, and an "emergent system," suggesting that the universe's properties cannot be merely reduced to its parts.This theory seems to offer a unified perspective on the universe, grounding its mysteries in the realm of quantum information. However, it would require rigorous mathematical backing and empirical evidence to gain mainstream acceptance in the scientific community.Entropy

By introducing the idea of information (using lnâ¡(2)\ln(2)ln(2) which relates to the information content of a bit), we're saying that energy and entropy (or information) are deeply linked.Example: Think of a gas in a chamber. As the gas molecules move and collide, they distribute energy and, by extension, information throughout the chamber. If we were to know the position and momentum of every molecule at a given time, we would have maximum information and minimum entropy. But as time progresses and the gas molecules move unpredictably, our uncertainty (or entropy) increases, representing a spread in the information we have about the system.These formulations and their conceptual implications suggest a deep intertwining of classical and quantum physics with information theory. ABSTRACT 
The dream of capturing the workings of the entire universe in a single equation or a simple set of 
equations is still pursued. A set of five new equivalent formulations of entropy based on the 
introduction of the mass of the information bit in Louis de Broglie's hidden thermodynamics and on 
the physicality of information, is proposed, within the framework of the emergent entangled 
informational universe model, which is based on the principle of strong emergence, the mass- 
energy-information equivalence principle and the Landauerâs principle. This model can explain 
various process as informational quantum processes such energy, dark matter, dark energy, 
cosmological constant and vacuum energy. The dark energy is explained as a collective potential of 
all particles with their individual zero-point energy emerging from an informational field, distinct from 
the usual fields of matter of quantum field theory, associated with dark matter as having a finite and 
quantifiable mass; while resolving the black hole information paradox by calculating the entropy of 
the entangled Hawking radiation, and shedding light on gravitational fine-grained entropy of black 
holes. This model explains the collapse of the wave function by the fact that a measure informs the 
measurer about the system to be measured and, this model is able to invalidate the many worlds 
interpretation of quantum mechanics and the simulation hypothesis.

This perspective attempts to offer a unified description of several phenomena in the cosmos, from dark matter and energy to the nature of entropy and the foundational principles of quantum mechanics.Here are my definitions of entropy: slice sameness, smoothness, isotropy, homogenous static noise, flatnessChatGPTYour definitions of entropy hint at the concept from various angles, emphasizing uniformity and lack of distinguishable structure. Let's break them down:Slice Sameness:This could refer to a system where every "slice" or segment of the system looks the same, reflecting a consistent, uniform state. It's the idea that if you were to segment or "slice" a system into multiple parts, each part would be identical in terms of its informational content.Smoothness:In the context of entropy, smoothness implies a lack of abrupt changes or differences in the system. A high entropy system would have a smooth gradient of change, while a low entropy system might display more abrupt or noticeable variations.Isotropy:Isotropy refers to the property of being identical in all directions. For entropy, this definition suggests that a high entropy system does not favor one direction over another; it's uniformly random and directionless.Homogeneous Static Noise:Homogeneity indicates uniformity. Coupled with "static noise," it refers to a kind of consistent randomness. Like the white noise on a detuned TV, where every part of the screen has an equal chance of being any given shade of gray, and there's no discernible pattern or structure.Flatness:This definition emphasizes the lack of peaks or valleys, or more generally, the absence of fluctuations or deviations from a mean state. In terms of entropy, this would represent a system in a state of maximal entropy where no further changes or fluctuations can increase its disorder.These definitions provide a holistic perspective on entropy, emphasizing its nature as a measure of disorder, uniformity, and randomness. Introduction to Relativistic Scalar Vector Plenum (RSVP) Theory

The cosmos, with its vast stretches of darkness punctuated by brilliant luminous bodies, has always posed questions that challenge the very essence of our understanding.

Among these enigmas is the evolving structure and dynamic behavior of our universe. While conventional theories suggest an expanding universe, the Relativistic Scalar Vector Plenum (RSVP) theory offers a different perspective, proposing that the universe itself remains static in size.

Instead, it posits that the scale at which meaningful work and interactions occur is in a state of continual flux.

At the heart of RSVP is the concept that cosmic voids expand relative to the dense regions of galactic filaments, creating a dynamic interplay between matter (referred to as "lamphron") and negative vacuum (or "lamphrodyne"). This interplay is crucial during the formation of the inflaton field.

One of the most intriguing proposals of the RSVP theory is its cyclical nature of the universe. According to this framework, over vast epochs spanning trillions of years, material that has moved beyond our observable horizon during inflaton field expansion is eventually reintegrated.

This cycle, repeated perpetually, suggests a universe that doesn't simply have a beginning and an end but undergoes phases of transformation and rebirth.

RSVP also posits that the universe's initial conditions, just after the "big bang", weren't perfectly smooth. Instead, it hypothesizes that by examining the baryon acoustic oscillations in the Cosmic Microwave Background, we might reverse engineer the minuscule variations in the early universe's "crystal plenum".ChatGPTThe Relativistic Scalar Vector Plenum (RSVP) Theory you've outlined introduces an innovative perspective on the cosmos, suggesting a continuous, cyclical universe where scales of interactions evolve over time. Let's see how your concepts connect to the previous topics discussed:Entropy & Universe:The universe's initial conditions, as described in RSVP, weren't perfectly smooth, echoing the notion of entropy as variations in homogeneity.The dynamic interplay between lamphron and lamphrodyne can be considered an informational dance where the universe constantly "rebalances" its entropy.PoincarÃ©'s Recurrence & Prigogine's Structures:The cyclical nature of RSVP aligns with PoincarÃ©'s idea of systems returning to initial states.Cosmic voids expanding relative to dense galactic regions reminds one of Prigogine's dissipative structures, where systems increase order using surrounding energy.Combinatory Logic:If the universe is defined by interplays between lamphron and lamphrodyne, then this interplay can be viewed as a form of computation. Here, the rules of this cosmic computation align with combinatorial logic.Gravitational Energy & Zero-Energy Universe:Your model presents the universe as one where energy dynamics between cosmic voids and galactic regions balance out.
